     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_evolutionary_history_of_life" title="Timeline of evolutionary history of life">
       Timeline of evolutionary history of life
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The evolutionary history of life stretches back to over
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3,000">
        3,000
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      , possibly as far as
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3,800">
        3,800
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PiP_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PiP-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
       Earth
      </a>
      formed about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=4,570">
        4,570
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      and, after a collision that formed the
      <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
       Moon
      </a>
      about 40 million years later, may have cooled quickly enough to have oceans and an atmosphere about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=4,440">
        4,440
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, there is evidence on the Moon of a
      <a href="/wiki/Late_Heavy_Bombardment" title="Late Heavy Bombardment">
       Late Heavy Bombardment
      </a>
      from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=40003800">
        4,000to3,800
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      . If, as seem likely, such a bombardment struck Earth at the same time, the first atmosphere and oceans may have been stripped away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The oldest clear evidence of life on Earth dates to
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3,000">
        3,000
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      , although there have been reports, often disputed, of
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">
       fossil
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">
       bacteria
      </a>
      from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3,400">
        3,400
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      and of geochemical evidence for the presence of life
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3,800">
        3,800
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrasierMcLoughlinEtAl2006FreshLook_9-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-BrasierMcLoughlinEtAl2006FreshLook-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some scientists have proposed that life on Earth was
      <a href="/wiki/Panspermia" title="Panspermia">
       "seeded" from elsewhere
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but most research concentrates on various explanations of how life could have
      <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">
       arisen independently
      </a>
      on Earth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Runzelmarken.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1852" data-file-width="3332" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Runzelmarken.jpg/250px-Runzelmarken.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Runzelmarken.jpg/375px-Runzelmarken.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Runzelmarken.jpg/500px-Runzelmarken.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Runzelmarken.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        This wrinkled "elephant skin" texture is a
        <a href="/wiki/Trace_fossil" title="Trace fossil">
         trace fossil
        </a>
        of a non-
        <a href="/wiki/Stromatolite" title="Stromatolite">
         stromatolite
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Microbial_mat" title="Microbial mat">
         microbial mat
        </a>
        .
        <br/>
        The image shows the location, in the
        <a href="/wiki/Burgsvik_beds" title="Burgsvik beds">
         Burgsvik beds
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">
         Sweden
        </a>
        , where the texture was first identified as evidence of a microbial mat.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manten1966_52-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Manten1966-52">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          52
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      For about 2,000 million years
      <a href="/wiki/Microbial_mat" title="Microbial mat">
       microbial mats
      </a>
      , multi-layered colonies of different types of bacteria, were the dominant life on Earth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KrumbeinBrehmEtAl2003BiofilmBiodictyonBiomatEtc_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-KrumbeinBrehmEtAl2003BiofilmBiodictyonBiomatEtc-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The evolution of
      <a href="/wiki/Oxygen#Photosynthesis_and_respiration" title="Oxygen">
       oxygenic photosynthesis
      </a>
      enabled them to play the major role in the
      <a href="/wiki/Oxygen#Build-up_in_the_atmosphere" title="Oxygen">
       oxygenation of the atmosphere
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoehlerBeboutMarais2001MicrobialMatsInProductionOfReducedGasesOnEarlyEarth_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HoehlerBeboutMarais2001MicrobialMatsInProductionOfReducedGasesOnEarlyEarth-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      from about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=2,400">
        2,400
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      . This change in the atmosphere increased their effectiveness as nurseries of evolution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NisbetFowler1999ArchaeanMetabolicEvolution_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NisbetFowler1999ArchaeanMetabolicEvolution-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While
      <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">
       eukaryotes
      </a>
      , cells with complex internal structures, may have been present earlier, their evolution speeded up when they acquired the ability to transform oxygen from a
      <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">
       poison
      </a>
      to a powerful source of energy in their
      <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">
       metabolism
      </a>
      . This innovation may have come from primitive eukaryotes capturing oxygen-powered bacteria as
      <a href="/wiki/Endosymbiont" title="Endosymbiont">
       endosymbionts
      </a>
      and transforming them into
      <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">
       organelles
      </a>
      called
      <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">
       mitochondria
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PiP_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-PiP-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earliest evidence of complex eukaryotes with organelles such as mitochondria, dates from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=1,850">
        1,850
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HedgesBlairEtAl2004molecularTimescaleOfEukaryoteEvolution_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HedgesBlairEtAl2004molecularTimescaleOfEukaryoteEvolution-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicellular" title="Multicellular">
       Multicellular
      </a>
      life is composed only of eukaryotic cells, and the earliest evidence for it is the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francevillian_Group_Fossil" title="Francevillian Group Fossil">
       Francevillian Group Fossils
      </a>
      from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=2,100">
        2,100
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albani_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-albani-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      although specialization of cells for different functions first appears between
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=1,430">
        1,430
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      (a possible
      <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">
       fungus
      </a>
      ) and
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=1,200">
        1,200
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      (a probable
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_alga" title="Red alga">
       red alga
      </a>
      ).
      <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">
       Sexual reproduction
      </a>
      may be a prerequisite for specialization of cells, as an asexual multicellular organism might be at risk of being taken over by rogue cells that retain the ability to reproduce.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butterfield2000Bangiomorpha_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Butterfield2000Bangiomorpha-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butterfield2005ProterozoicFungi_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Butterfield2005ProterozoicFungi-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opabinia_BW2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Opabinia_BW2.jpg/150px-Opabinia_BW2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Opabinia_BW2.jpg/225px-Opabinia_BW2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Opabinia_BW2.jpg/300px-Opabinia_BW2.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opabinia_BW2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Opabinia" title="Opabinia">
          Opabinia
         </a>
        </i>
        made the largest single contribution to modern interest in the
        <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">
         Cambrian explosion
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The earliest known
      <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">
       animals
      </a>
      are
      <a href="/wiki/Cnidaria" title="Cnidaria">
       cnidarians
      </a>
      from about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=580">
        580
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      , but these are so modern-looking that the earliest animals must have appeared before then.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Early fossils of animals are rare because they did not develop
      <a href="/wiki/Biomineralization" title="Biomineralization">
       mineralized
      </a>
      hard parts that fossilize easily until about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=548">
        548
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bengtson2004_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bengtson2004-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earliest modern-looking
      <a href="/wiki/Bilateria" title="Bilateria">
       bilaterian
      </a>
      animals appear in the Early
      <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">
       Cambrian
      </a>
      , along with several "weird wonders" that bear little obvious resemblance to any modern animals. There is a long-running debate about whether this
      <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">
       Cambrian explosion
      </a>
      was truly a very rapid period of evolutionary experimentation; alternative views are that modern-looking animals began evolving earlier but fossils of their precursors have not yet been found, or that the "weird wonders" are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stem_group" title="Stem group">
       evolutionary "aunts" and "cousins"
      </a>
      of modern groups.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006Explaining_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006Explaining-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebrates" title="Vertebrates">
       Vertebrates
      </a>
      remained an obscure group until the first fish with jaws appeared in the Late
      <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">
       Ordovician
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The spread of life from water to land required organisms to solve several problems, including protection against drying out and supporting themselves against
      <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">
       gravity
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garwood_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Garwood-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selden2001TerrestrializationOfAnimals_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Selden2001TerrestrializationOfAnimals-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KenrickCrane1997EvolutionOfLandPlants_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-KenrickCrane1997EvolutionOfLandPlants-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earliest evidence of land plants and land invertebrates date back to about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=476">
        476
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      and
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=490">
        490
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KenrickCrane1997EvolutionOfLandPlants_67-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-KenrickCrane1997EvolutionOfLandPlants-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The lineage that produced land vertebrates evolved later but very rapidly between
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=370">
        370
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      and
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=360">
        360
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      recent discoveries have overturned earlier ideas about the history and driving forces behind their evolution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clack2005GettingLegUp_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Clack2005GettingLegUp-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Land plants were so successful that they caused an
      <a href="/wiki/Ecological_crisis" title="Ecological crisis">
       ecological crisis
      </a>
      in the Late
      <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">
       Devonian
      </a>
      , until the evolution and spread of fungi that could digest dead wood.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeoScheckler1998errestrialMarineTeleconnectionsInDevonian_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-AlgeoScheckler1998errestrialMarineTeleconnectionsInDevonian-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yanoconodon_BW.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="800" height="51" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yanoconodon_BW.jpg/150px-Yanoconodon_BW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yanoconodon_BW.jpg/225px-Yanoconodon_BW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Yanoconodon_BW.jpg/300px-Yanoconodon_BW.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yanoconodon_BW.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        At about 13 centimetres (5.1in) the Early Cretaceous
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Yanoconodon" title="Yanoconodon">
          Yanoconodon
         </a>
        </i>
        was longer than the average mammal of the time.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-_72-0">
         <a href="#cite_note--72">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          72
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:House_sparrow04.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/House_sparrow04.jpg/220px-House_sparrow04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/House_sparrow04.jpg/330px-House_sparrow04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/House_sparrow04.jpg/440px-House_sparrow04.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:House_sparrow04.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">
         Birds
        </a>
        are the last surviving
        <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">
         dinosaurs
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-padian2004_73-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-padian2004-73">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          73
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the
      <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">
       Permian
      </a>
      period
      <a href="/wiki/Synapsid" title="Synapsid">
       synapsids
      </a>
      , including the ancestors of
      <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">
       mammals
      </a>
      , may have dominated land environments,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but the
      <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="PermianTriassic extinction event">
       PermianTriassic extinction event
      </a>
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=251">
        251
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      came very close to wiping out complex life.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The extinctions were apparently fairly sudden, at least among vertebrates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the slow recovery from this catastrophe a previously obscure group,
      <a href="/wiki/Archosaur" title="Archosaur">
       archosaurs
      </a>
      , became the most abundant and diverse terrestrial vertebrates. One archosaur group, the
      <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">
       dinosaurs
      </a>
      , were the dominant land vertebrates for the rest of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">
       Mesozoic
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">
       birds
      </a>
      evolved from one group of dinosaurs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-padian2004_73-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-padian2004-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During this time mammals' ancestors survived only as small, mainly nocturnal
      <a href="/wiki/Insectivore" title="Insectivore">
       insectivores
      </a>
      , but this apparent set-back may have accelerated the development of mammalian traits such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endothermy" title="Endothermy">
       endothermy
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hair" title="Hair">
       hair
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RubenJones2000FurAndFeathers_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RubenJones2000FurAndFeathers-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the
      <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="CretaceousPaleogene extinction event">
       CretaceousPaleogene extinction event
      </a>
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=65">
        65
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      killed off the non-avian dinosaurs birds are the only surviving dinosaurs mammals increased rapidly in size and diversity, and some took to the air and the sea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg/200px-Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg/300px-Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg/400px-Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bee_pollinating_a_rose.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A modern
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_insect" title="Social insect">
         social insect
        </a>
        collects pollen from a modern
        <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">
         flowering plant
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Fossil evidence indicates that
      <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">
       flowering plants
      </a>
      appeared and rapidly diversified in the Early
      <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">
       Cretaceous
      </a>
      , between
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=130">
        130
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      and
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=90">
        90
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CraneFriisPedersen2000OriginAndDiversificationOfAngiosperms_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CraneFriisPedersen2000OriginAndDiversificationOfAngiosperms-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Their rapid rise to dominance of terrestrial ecosystems is thought to have been propelled by
      <a href="/wiki/Coevolution" title="Coevolution">
       coevolution
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Pollination" title="Pollination">
       pollinating
      </a>
      insects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crepet2000_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Crepet2000-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_insects" title="Social insects">
       Social insects
      </a>
      appeared around the same time and, although they account for only small parts of the insect "family tree", now form over 50% of the total mass of all insects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilsonH.C3.B6lldobler2005EusocialityOriginConsequences_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WilsonH.C3.B6lldobler2005EusocialityOriginConsequences-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Humans evolved from a lineage of upright-walking
      <a href="/wiki/Ape" title="Ape">
       apes
      </a>
      whose earliest fossils date from over
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=6">
        6
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although early members of this lineage had
      <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee" title="Chimpanzee">
       chimp
      </a>
      -sized
      <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">
       brains
      </a>
      , about 25% as big as modern humans', there are signs of a steady increase in brain size after about
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=3">
        3
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There is a long-running debate about whether
      <i>
       modern
      </i>
      humans are descendants of a
      <a href="/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Recent African origin of modern humans">
       single small population in Africa
      </a>
      , which then migrated all over the world less than 200,000 years ago and replaced previous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hominine" title="Hominine">
       hominine
      </a>
      species, or
      <a href="/wiki/Multiregional_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Multiregional origin of modern humans">
       arose worldwide at the same time
      </a>
      as a result of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interbreeding" title="Interbreeding">
       interbreeding
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_extinctions">
       Mass extinctions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paleontology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mass extinctions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>

          </a>
         </span>
        </div>

          </span>

        <div id="annotation_115x235" style="position:absolute; left:115px; top:235px; font-weight:normal; line-height:110%">

         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_312x135" style="position:absolute; left:312px; top:135px; line-height:110%">

           </small>

          </a>
         </span>
        </div>

          </a>
         </span>
        </div>

        </div>

          </a>

          </a>
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="visibility:hidden">
        <div class="noresize">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Extinction_intensity.svg" title="File:Extinction intensity.svg">
          <img alt="Extinction intensity.svg" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="531" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/320px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/480px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/640px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_1_245216671" width="320"/>

          </area>
          <area alt="Permian" coords="151,0,178,14" href="/wiki/Permian" shape="rect" title="Permian">
          </area>

          </area>

         </map>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumbcaption" style="width:330px;">
       Apparent extinction intensity, i.e. the fraction of
       <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">
        genera
       </a>
       going extinct at any given time, as reconstructed from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_record" title="Fossil record">
        fossil record
       </a>
       (graph not meant to include recent epoch of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction_event" title="Holocene extinction event">
        Holocene extinction event
       </a>
       )
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" title="Mass extinction">
       Mass extinction
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Life on earth has suffered occasional mass extinctions at least since
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=542">
        542
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      . Although they are disasters at the time, mass extinctions have sometimes accelerated the evolution of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_earth" title="Life on earth">
       life on earth
      </a>
      . When dominance of particular
      <a href="/wiki/Ecological_niche" title="Ecological niche">
       ecological niches
      </a>
      passes from one group of organisms to another, it is rarely because the new dominant group is "superior" to the old and usually because an extinction event eliminates the old dominant group and makes way for the new one.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fossil record appears to show that the rate of extinction is slowing down, with both the gaps between mass extinctions becoming longer and the average and background rates of extinction decreasing. However, it is not certain whether the actual rate of extinction has altered, since both of these observations could be explained in several ways:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacLeod2001Extinction_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MacLeod2001Extinction-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The oceans may have become more hospitable to life over the last 500million years and less vulnerable to mass extinctions:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissolved_oxygen" title="Dissolved oxygen">
        dissolved oxygen
       </a>
       became more widespread and penetrated to greater depths; the development of life on land reduced the run-off of nutrients and hence the risk of
       <a href="/wiki/Eutrophication" title="Eutrophication">
        eutrophication
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Anoxic_event" title="Anoxic event">
        anoxic events
       </a>
       ; marine ecosystems became more diversified so that
       <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">
        food chains
       </a>
       were less likely to be disrupted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         91
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         92
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Reasonably complete
       <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">
        fossils
       </a>
       are very rare, most extinct organisms are represented only by partial fossils, and complete fossils are rarest in the oldest rocks. So paleontologists have mistakenly assigned parts of the same organism to different
       <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">
        genera
       </a>
       , which were often defined solely to accommodate these finds the story of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Anomalocaris" title="Anomalocaris">
         Anomalocaris
        </a>
       </i>
       is an example of this.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WonderfulLifeP194To206_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WonderfulLifeP194To206-93">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         93
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The risk of this mistake is higher for older fossils because these are often unlike parts of any living organism. Many "superfluous" genera are represented by fragments that are not found again, and these "superfluous" genera appear to become extinct very quickly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacLeod2001Extinction_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-MacLeod2001Extinction-90">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         90
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <div class="thumb" style="float:right; clear:right; margin-left:5px; border:solid #ccc 1px; padding:2px; width:308px;;">
      <div class="thumbinner image" style="position:relative; width:300px; height:180px; border:solid #ccc 1px; background-color:white;">
       <div style=";left:0px; top:0px; width:300px; position:absolute;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png" title="Phanerozoic biodiversity as shown by the fossil record">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="784" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/300px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/450px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/600px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div style="text-align:left; background-color:transparent; line-height:110%;">
        <div id="annotation_20x0" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:0px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          All
          <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">
           genera
          </a>
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_20x14" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:14px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          "Well-defined" genera
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_20x28" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:28px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          Trend line
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_20x42" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:42px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          "Big Five"
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" title="Mass extinction">
           mass extinctions
          </a>
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_20x56" style="position:absolute; left:20px; top:56px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          Other mass extinctions
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_50x165" style="position:absolute; left:50px; top:165px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          Million years ago
         </span>
        </div>
        <div id="annotation_180x165" style="position:absolute; left:180px; top:165px; line-height:110%">
         <span style="background-color:transparent;">
          Thousands of genera
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="visibility:hidden">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="464" data-file-width="784" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/300px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/450px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6b/Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png/600px-Phanerozoic_biodiversity_blank_01.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumbcaption" style="width:300px;">
       Phanerozoic biodiversity as shown by the fossil record
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">
       Biodiversity
      </a>
      in the fossil record, which is
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <dl>
        <dd>
         "the number of distinct genera alive at any given time; that is, those whose first occurrence predates and whose last occurrence postdates that time"
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RohdeMuller2005_94-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-RohdeMuller2005-94">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           94
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </dd>
       </dl>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      shows a different trend: a fairly swift rise from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=542400">
        542to400
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      , a slight decline from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=400200">
        400to200
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      , in which the devastating
      <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="PermianTriassic extinction event">
       PermianTriassic extinction event
      </a>
      is an important factor, and a swift rise from
      <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=200">
        200
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
        million years ago
       </a>
      </span>
      to the present.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RohdeMuller2005_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RohdeMuller2005-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_paleontology">
       History of paleontology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paleontology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: History of paleontology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_paleontology" title="History of paleontology">
       History of paleontology
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_paleontology" title="Timeline of paleontology">
       Timeline of paleontology
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="638" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg/200px-Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg/300px-Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg/400px-Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuvier_elephant_jaw.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        This illustration of an
        <a href="/wiki/Indian_elephant" title="Indian elephant">
         Indian elephant
        </a>
        jaw and a
        <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">
         mammoth
        </a>
        jaw (top) is from
        <a href="/wiki/Georges_Cuvier" title="Georges Cuvier">
         Cuvier
        </a>
        's 1796 paper on living and fossil elephants.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Although paleontology became established around 1800, earlier thinkers had noticed aspects of the
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">
       fossil
      </a>
      record. The ancient Greek
      <a href="/wiki/Philosophy#Ancient_philosophy" title="Philosophy">
       philosopher
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Xenophanes" title="Xenophanes">
       Xenophanes
      </a>
      (570480 BC) concluded from fossil sea shells that some areas of land were once under water.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
       Middle Ages
      </a>
      the Persian naturalist
      <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">
       Ibn Sina
      </a>
      , known as
      <i>
       Avicenna
      </i>
      in Europe, discussed fossils and proposed a theory of petrifying fluids on which
      <a href="/wiki/Albert_of_Saxony_(philosopher)" title="Albert of Saxony (philosopher)">
       Albert of Saxony
      </a>
      elaborated in the 14th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Chinese naturalist
      <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">
       Shen Kuo
      </a>
      (10311095) proposed a theory of climate change based on the presence of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrified" title="Petrified">
       petrified
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">
       bamboo
      </a>
      in regions that in his time were too dry for bamboo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Europe" title="Early modern Europe">
       early modern Europe
      </a>
      , the systematic study of fossils emerged as an integral part of the changes in
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_philosophy" title="Natural philosophy">
       natural philosophy
      </a>
      that occurred during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Reason" title="Age of Reason">
       Age of Reason
      </a>
      . At the end of the 18th century
      <a href="/wiki/Georges_Cuvier" title="Georges Cuvier">
       Georges Cuvier
      </a>
      's work established
      <a href="/wiki/Comparative_anatomy" title="Comparative anatomy">
       comparative anatomy
      </a>
      as a scientific discipline and, by proving that some fossil animals resembled no living ones, demonstrated that animals could become
      <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">
       extinct
      </a>
      , leading to the emergence of paleontology.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The expanding knowledge of the fossil record also played an increasing role in the development of
      <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">
       geology
      </a>
      , particularly
      <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy" title="Stratigraphy">
       stratigraphy
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palmer2005EarthTime_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Palmer2005EarthTime-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first half of the 19th century saw geological and paleontological activity become increasingly well organized with the growth of geologic societies and museums
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and an increasing number of professional geologists and fossil specialists. Interest increased for reasons that were not purely scientific, as geology and paleontology helped industrialists to find and exploit natural resources such as
      <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">
       coal
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      This contributed to a rapid increase in knowledge about the history of life on Earth and to progress in the definition of the
      <a href="/wiki/Geologic_time_scale" title="Geologic time scale">
       geologic time scale
      </a>
      , largely based on fossil evidence. In 1822 Henri Marie Ducrotay de Blanville, editor of
      <i>
       Journal de Phisique
      </i>
      , coined the word "palaeontology" to refer to the study of ancient living organisms through fossils.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As knowledge of life's history continued to improve, it became increasingly obvious that there had been some kind of successive order to the development of life. This encouraged early evolutionary theories on the
      <a href="/wiki/Transmutation_of_species" title="Transmutation of species">
       transmutation of species
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BucklandGould_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BucklandGould-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">
       Charles Darwin
      </a>
      published
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_Species" title="Origin of Species">
        Origin of Species
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1859, much of the focus of paleontology shifted to understanding
      <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">
       evolutionary
      </a>
      paths, including
      <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">
       human evolution
      </a>
      , and evolutionary theory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BucklandGould_104-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BucklandGould-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haikouichthys4.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="500" height="60" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Haikouichthys4.png/200px-Haikouichthys4.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Haikouichthys4.png/300px-Haikouichthys4.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Haikouichthys4.png/400px-Haikouichthys4.png 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haikouichthys4.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Haikouichthys" title="Haikouichthys">
          Haikouichthys
         </a>
        </i>
        , from about
        <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=518">
          518
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Myr" title="Myr">
          million years ago
         </a>
        </span>
        in China, may be the earliest known fish.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
         <a href="#cite_note-105">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          105
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The last half of the 19th century saw a tremendous expansion in paleontological activity, especially in
      <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
       North America
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trend continued in the 20th century with additional regions of the Earth being opened to systematic fossil collection. Fossils found in China near the end of the 20th century have been particularly important as they have provided new information about the earliest evolution of
      <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">
       animals
      </a>
      , early
      <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">
       fish
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">
       dinosaurs
      </a>
      and the evolution of birds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The last few decades of the 20th century saw a renewed interest in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_extinction" title="Mass extinction">
       mass extinctions
      </a>
      and their role in the evolution of life on Earth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There was also a renewed interest in the
      <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">
       Cambrian explosion
      </a>
      that apparently saw the development of the body plans of most animal
      <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">
       phyla
      </a>
      . The discovery of fossils of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ediacaran_biota" title="Ediacaran biota">
       Ediacaran biota
      </a>
      and developments in
      <a href="/wiki/Paleobiology" title="Paleobiology">
       paleobiology
      </a>
      extended knowledge about the history of life back far before the Cambrian.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006Explaining_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006Explaining-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Increasing awareness of
      <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Mendel" title="Gregor Mendel">
       Gregor Mendel
      </a>
      's pioneering work in
      <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">
       genetics
      </a>
      led first to the development of
      <a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">
       population genetics
      </a>
      and then in the mid-20th century to the
      <a href="/wiki/Modern_evolutionary_synthesis" title="Modern evolutionary synthesis">
       modern evolutionary synthesis
      </a>
      , which explains
      <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">
       evolution
      </a>
      as the outcome of events such as
      <a href="/wiki/Mutation" title="Mutation">
       mutations
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_gene_transfer" title="Horizontal gene transfer">
       horizontal gene transfer
      </a>
      , which provide
      <a href="/wiki/Genetic_variation" title="Genetic variation">
       genetic variation
      </a>
      , with
      <a href="/wiki/Genetic_drift" title="Genetic drift">
       genetic drift
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">
       natural selection
      </a>
      driving changes in this variation over time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Within the next few years the role and operation of
      <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">
       DNA
      </a>
      in genetic inheritance were discovered, leading to what is now known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Central_dogma_of_molecular_biology" title="Central dogma of molecular biology">
       "Central Dogma" of molecular biology
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the 1960s
      <a href="/wiki/Molecular_phylogenetics" title="Molecular phylogenetics">
       molecular phylogenetics
      </a>
      , the investigation of evolutionary "family trees" by techniques derived from
      <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">
       biochemistry
      </a>
      , began to make an impact, particularly when it was proposed that the human lineage had diverged from
      <a href="/wiki/Ape" title="Ape">
       apes
      </a>
      much more recently than was generally thought at the time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although this early study compared
      <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">
       proteins
      </a>
      from apes and humans, most molecular phylogenetics research is now based on comparisons of
      <a href="/wiki/RNA" title="RNA">
       RNA
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">
       DNA
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
       See also
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paleontology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: See also">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="noprint portal tright" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em">
